This incompatibility occurs due to pandas' automatic dtype inference logic that cannot represent NA values in standard NumPy integer dtypes.\n\n## Root Cause Analysis\n\n### Primary Issue Location\n**File**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py`\n**Function**: `to_numpy_dtype_inference()`\n**Lines**: 35-52 (critical logic at lines 41-42)\n\n### Root Cause Code\n```python\ndef to_numpy_dtype_inference(\n    arr: ExtensionArray,\n    dtype: npt.DTypeLike | None,\n    na_value,\n    hasna: bool,\n) -> tuple[np.dtype | None, Any]:\n    result_dtype: np.dtype | None\n    inferred_numeric_dtype = False\n    if dtype is None and is_numeric_dtype(arr.dtype):\n        inferred_numeric_dtype = True\n        if hasna:\n            if arr.dtype.kind == \"b\":\n                result_dtype = np.dtype(np.object_)\n            else:\n                if arr.dtype.kind in \"iu\":  # <-- INTEGER CHECK\n                    result_dtype = np.dtype(np.float64)  # <-- FORCED CONVERSION TO FLOAT64\n                else:\n                    result_dtype = arr.dtype.numpy_dtype\n```\n\n**The Problem**: When a nullable integer array has missing values (`hasna=True`) and the dtype kind is \"i\" (signed integer) or \"u\" (unsigned integer), the function automatically converts the target dtype to `np.float64` (line 42). This occurs because standard NumPy integer dtypes cannot represent NA values. This incompatibility occurs due to pandas' automatic dtype inference logic that cannot represent NA values in standard NumPy integer dtypes.\n\n## Root Cause Analysis\n\n### Primary Issue Location\n**File**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py`\n**Function**: `to_numpy_dtype_inference()`\n**Lines**: 35-52 (critical logic at lines 41-42)\n\n### Root Cause Code\n```python\ndef to_numpy_dtype_inference(\n    arr: ExtensionArray,\n    dtype: npt.DTypeLike | None,\n    na_value,\n    hasna: bool,\n) -> tuple[np.dtype | None, Any]:\n    result_dtype: np.dtype | None\n    inferred_numeric_dtype = False\n    if dtype is None and is_numeric_dtype(arr.dtype):\n        inferred_numeric_dtype = True\n        if hasna:\n            if arr.dtype.kind == \"b\":\n                result_dtype = np.dtype(np.object_)\n            else:\n                if arr.dtype.kind in \"iu\":  # <-- INTEGER CHECK\n                    result_dtype = np.dtype(np.float64)  # <-- FORCED CONVERSION TO FLOAT64\n                else:\n                    result_dtype = arr.dtype.numpy_dtype\n```\n\n**The Problem**: When a nullable integer array has missing values (`hasna=True`) and the dtype kind is \"i\" (signed integer) or \"u\" (unsigned integer), the function automatically converts the target dtype to `np.float64` (line 42). This is because NumPy's standard integer dtypes cannot represent NA values, so pandas defaults to float64 as a container that can hold both numbers and NaN.\n\n### Secondary Issue Location\n**File**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/masked.py`\n**Method**: `__array__()`\n**Lines**: 694-716\n\n### Secondary Issue Code\n```python\ndef __array__(\n    self, dtype: NpDtype | None = None, copy: bool | None = None\n) -> np.ndarray:\n    \"\"\"\n    the array interface, return my values\n    We return an object array here to preserve our scalar values\n    \"\"\"\n    if copy is False:\n        if not self._hasna:\n            # special case, here we can simply return the underlying data\n            result = np.array(self._data, dtype=dtype, copy=copy)\n            if self._readonly:\n                result = result.view()\n                result.flags.writeable = False\n            return result\n        raise ValueError(\n            \"Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\"\n        )\n\n    if copy is None:\n        copy = False  # The NumPy copy=False meaning is different here.\n    return self.to_numpy(dtype=dtype, copy=copy)  # <-- CALLS to_numpy_dtype_inference\n```\n\n**The Problem**: The `__array__` method (which is called by NumPy's array protocol when converting pandas arrays to NumPy arrays) delegates dtype handling to `to_numpy()`, which then applies the automatic dtype inference. When NA values are present and no explicit dtype is provided, this results in the unwanted float64 conversion.\n\n## Data Flow: From DataFrame to NumPy Array\n\n1. **scikit-learn preprocessing receives DataFrame**\n   - The preprocessing functions attempt to convert the DataFrame to a NumPy array\n\n3. **NumPy's Array Protocol Invoked**\n   - NumPy calls the `__array__()` method on the pandas ExtensionArray\n   - Location: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/masked.py`, line 694\n\n4. **__array__ delegates to to_numpy()**\n   - Location: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/masked.py`, line 716\n   - Calls: `self.to_numpy(dtype=dtype, copy=copy)`\n\n5. **to_numpy() method invokes dtype inference**\n   - Location: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/masked.py`, line 512\n   - Calls: `to_numpy_dtype_inference(self, dtype, na_value, hasna)` at line 579\n\n6. **Root Cause: Automatic dtype conversion**\n   - Location: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py`, lines 41-42\n   - **Decision point**: When `dtype is None` and array has NA values and kind is \"iu\" (integer)\n   - **Action**: Automatically sets `result_dtype = np.dtype(np.float64)`\n   - **Reasoning**: NumPy standard integer dtypes cannot represent NA values, so float64 is used as a container that can hold both numbers and NaN\n\n7. **Array Conversion with Unexpected Dtype**\n   - The array is converted to float64 instead of the expected integer type\n   - Missing values are converted to `np.nan`\n   - Original dtype information is lost\n\n8. **scikit-learn Receives Wrong Dtype**\n   - StandardScaler/MinMaxScaler expects: integer array or float array with specific properties\n   - Receives: float64 array with NaN values (which may cause issues in preprocessing calculations)\n\n## Incompatibility Issues\n\n### Issue 1: Unexpected dtype transformation\n- **Expected**: Int64 array\n- **Actual**: float64 array\n- **Impact**: Algorithms that check `dtype.kind` may behave differently\n\n### Issue 2: Data representation change\n- Original data uses NA (pandas' null value)\n- After conversion: uses np.nan (NumPy's float NaN)\n- Different semantics for missing value handling\n\n### Issue 3: Memory and performance implications\n- int64: 8 bytes per value\n- float64: 8 bytes per value (same memory) but different computational behavior\n- Float operations may be slower or less accurate than integer operations in preprocessing\n\n### Issue 4: Scikit-learn validation issues\n- scikit-learn's input validation may expect integer dtypes to remain integers\n- May reject or improperly handle the automatic float64 conversion\n- Could cause preprocessing to fail or produce incorrect results\n\n## Affected Code Paths\n\n### Path 1: DataFrame Conversion (Most Common)\n```\nDataFrame with Int64 column\n→ np.asarray(dataframe)\n→ Column's __array__() method (masked.py:694)\n→ to_numpy() (masked.py:512)\n→ to_numpy_dtype_inference() (_utils.py:27)\n→ Auto-convert to float64 (_utils.py:41-42)\n→ Incompatibility with scikit-learn\n```\n\n### Path 2: Direct Array Conversion\n```\nSeries with Int64Dtype and NA values\n→ np.asarray(series.values)\n→ __array__() (masked.py:694)\n→ to_numpy_dtype_inference() (_utils.py:27)\n→ Auto-convert to float64 (_utils.py:41-42)\n```\n\n## NumPy Interaction\n**File**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/numpy/numpy/_core/_methods.py`\n\nWhile NumPy itself doesn't explicitly cause the issue, its array protocol (`__array__` interface) is the mechanism through which the incompatibility manifests.
